Set chip->initialized = 1\n\nThe problem is that if chip->single_cmd is still 1 from a previous error, it won't call azx_init_cmd_io to reinitialize the ring buffers. Still timeout -> switch to single_cmd mode\n\nOnce in single_cmd mode, the driver uses a different command mechanism (not CORB/RIRB). The issue is that this state persists across suspend/resume. When resuming, azx_init_chip is called with full_reset=1, which checks if chip->initialized is 0 and continues with azx_reset, but the single_cmd and polling_mode flags remain set from the error recovery sequence.\n\nThe problem becomes apparent during the initialization check: if single_cmd is already 1, the code skips azx_init_cmd_io and doesn't reinitialize the ring buffers. While single_cmd mode uses the immediate command interface instead, there may be hardware state or other initialization that's not properly restored after resume. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016QnEuugvnzp8DGq2bNaMPK","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"OK so azx_reset resets the hardware by clearing and then setting the ICH6_GCTL_RESET bit. This brings the hardware to a known state. After reset, at line 1105-1107:```cif (!chip->single_cmd)    azx_writel(chip, GCTL, azx_readl(chip, GCTL) |               ICH6_GCTL_UNSOL);\n```\n\nIf single_cmd is 0, it enables unsolicited responses. If single_cmd is 1, it doesn't.\n\nSo the hardware resets to a default state, but then if chip->single_cmd is 1, it doesn't enable unsolicited responses. But this is based on the SOFTWARE state (chip->single_cmd), not the actual hardware state after reset.\n\nAfter a hardware reset, the controller should be back to ring buffer mode by default. So if chip->single_cmd is 1 (from a previous error), but the hardware is in ring buffer mode (after reset), there's a mismatch!\n\nThis is the bug!
